I serve with fresh bread and a simple salad.

text:
I've been making this sauce for years. I've used several different pastas - penne, tortellini, raviolis, any pasta that "holds" the sauce, b/c its so delish (oh, long fusilli works very well too!) I tried it this time with the pancetta as recipe stated and it was good, but I prefer prosciutto (what mom & nana used). I also add minced onion to the prosciutto while sauteing' & 1 tbls butter; also, I (not nana) use fat-free half & half, which makes absolutely no difference!  It's also great sans prosciutto/pancetta. In lieu of the shrimp, you can also try grilled chicken strips (my fav!)

I have made this twice now, and highly agree with the people who say the pancetta makes or breaks this recipe!  The first time I used a high quality pancetta that I bought from our Whole Foods store and it was OUTSTANDING! The second time, I used pre-packaged pancetta that I got from our local Walmart, and it turned out only eh,ok, not quite the same quality as it was the first time. With that said, I cant see how substituting bacon for the pancetta would even begin to give this the flavor it needs to be a superb dish. Will definately make again and again, but only when I am using the high quality pancetta!

Display Name:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/3651652.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
You will not find a better vodka sauce that's easier to make...you might not find a better vodka sauce, period. We prefer chunks of pancetta (or prosciutto) to thin-sliced, and our local Acme sells Daniele brand diced pancetta in 4oz. containers; we use one container per batch. Note: when using pre-diced meat, the fat is not trimmed; cut down on the butter by half or it'll get greasy. If you're dicing your own meat, trim off the fat and keep the butter, or keep 
a little fat for flavor and adjust the butter accordingly. A 1/2 cup of diced red onion (per batch) goes in with the pancetta, and Rao's marinara is the sauce of choice. Smirnoff vodka. Heavy cream. Parmesan goes right into the pot after the sauce is finished simmering, and some shaved Parmesan goes on top along with lots of fresh Italian parsley or basil. We always triple the recipe and freeze what we don't eat so it's ready to go the next time the craving hits. Because the craving always returns ?? Thanks, Rick!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was a hit with the bf. Substitutions and additions: I used Tinkada gluten-free rice Penne, cooked for 15 minutes instead of regular Penne. Tito's vodka was awesome in it and less pricey than Goose. Full fat heavy cream and Boar's Head Pancetta. For extra flavor, I added to the recipe 2 cloves of garlic, one small onion and half a small, red bell pepper, all minced together in a food processor. I added these ingredients after reducing the vodka and pancetta mixture. I also added about 2 cups of frozen jumbo peeled shrimp: defrosted in a pyrex in the sink with cold running water for about 15 minutes and then strained, placed back into pyrex and flash cooked in boiling water (just pour over them) until cooked through. Since the shrimp will float out of the container unless weighted, I keep a small sieve over them to keep them in the pyrex and keep the h2O flowing. Add the cooked shrimp and sauce to the Penne and cook 5 more minutes to allow flavors to meld. Sprinkled individual servings with fresh-grated parmegiano-regiano and fresh-ground black pepper. I served this with a spinach salad with toasted pecans, chevre and homemade shallot/red wine vinaigrette, and a nice Red Zinfandel.

The sauce turned out really good!  I did add some additional ingredients and we all loved the final outcome!  I made some bacon & seasoned chicken to add to the pasta/sauce and sauteed some chopped onions and mushrooms in the butter with some garlic.  I also  added some peas, sundried tomatoes, boursin garlic & herb cheese (because we had some) and basil.  Very good - especially with garlic bread! The only change I would make next time is to make extra sauce.  Bon Appetit!

text:
I've made this twice now, once with store bought sauce, and one with homemade. Both were excellent.the one thing I disliked was the pancetta floating in about 4 tbs of fat, so, while I understand wanting to soften the taste with butter, I drained the pan before adding the vodka. Everyone in my household loves this dish, and they get a kick out of the vodka as ingredient. (For those of you wary of the vodka, I assure you that you don't taste it, it simply adds flavor to the pancetta and helps finish off its cooking). Lovely, creamy, oh and USE AS LITTLE SALT AS POSSIBLE if you make your own sauce. Between the pancetta and the Parmesan you're all set.

text:
I combined this recipe and the "Tomato Vodka Sauce" recipe and it was as good as the sauce at my favorite little Italian place. Seperately, both of these recipes are OKAY but missing something. Comibing them did the trick. I made my own sauce with a 28oz can of chunky crushed tomatoes and a smaller can of diced tomatoes. I added chicken (2 breasts) and cooked it in 2TBSP of butter with 1T olive oil, one small onion diced, and 1 garlic clove finely chopped until the chicken was brown on the outisde and the pancetta was browning. I added the Vodka (1/2C) and after a few minutes the tomato products and whipping cream. I used more than 1/2C because I used more ingredients and wanted more sauce. I simmered it and topped it with Parm to serve.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I made this recipe two times.   The first time was excellent but I added too red pepper flakes (advice from another recipe).   This time I made the following changes:
1. Used 3/4 cup vodka infused with 1/4 tsp red pepper flakes.   The first time I used a tsp and way too much because I didn't strain out the flakes before adding to sauce.   This time 1/4 tsp didn't add enough kick, so I added two or three pinches to the final sauce and that proved to be just right.
2.  I fried the pancetta with two shallots minced and two cloves of minced garlic.
3.  I added freshly grated Parmesan cheese (about 1/2 cup) after sauce had simmered.
4.  I added fresh basil leaves (about five or six leaves) torn into smaller pieces.   This in my opinion adds an immense amount of flavor.
5.  I used plum tomatoes flavored with basil the first time.  This time I used crushed tomatoes and added three small fresh vine tomatoes coarsely chopped.  We like the texture of the sauce with chunky tomatoes.  I simmer my sauce longer (about 30 - 45 minutes) to get full flavor.

Instead of bacon I used sausage as the meat. Pretty tasty. I don't like chunky sauces so that's why I wanted to try this recipe. At first, the sauce tastes like really creamy tomato soup, which I didn't like. Then by the time the sauce simmered, the taste changed to more vodka sauce.  I have had it for leftovers twice now and I think it's even better reheated than fresh. I also used Romano on top instead of Parmesan. Not the very best of the best, but pretty good for it being so simple and easy to make, especially for those who don't like a bunch of stuff in their sauce.

text:
I absolutely LOVE this recipe, and it has unfortunately, ruined me for any other restaurant vodka sauce as none of them are good enough.  I have made this recipe countless of times for family and guests but always with the same disclaimer that they are not allowed to watch me make this as it's just not very healthy.  I've used 5-6 slices of chopped hickory smoked bacon in this recipe  in lieu of pancetta, and it tastes great.  I've found that the type of Vodka that you use really affects the taste.  You don't need to use expensive vodka to make it taste good.  (I use Vikingfjord and it tastes good to me.)  Unfortunately, I think heavy cream is the key to this recipe as I've tried to gone the healthy route and use regular cream and half and half - and it just doesn't taste as rich.

LOVE this recipe.  Just don't make it all the time, unless you work out a lot. :)

text:
I have made this recipe twice.  Once was as written and the second time with a few modifications.  It is good but slightly bland as written.  

First, it needs to be doubled.  I like to be generous with sauce and I like leftovers.  Next, add a little garlic.  And last, I used tomato sauce with italian seasoning or you can add your own to the sauce.  Don't add salt because it does not need it.  If you have enough for leftovers, it will be even better the next day.

text:
BETTER THAN ANY RESTAURANT! I doubled the sauce recipe after reading that advice in other reviews.  I'm glad I did.  I think the recipe as written would not make enough sauce for a whole pound of pasta.  Plus, the sauce tastes so good, you'll want plenty of it to dip your bread in. The sauce turned out great!  I added the following while I was browning the pancetta: 1/2 a large onion (chopped), 1 package sliced mushrooms, 1 can of peas (drained), 4 large cloves of garlic (minced), 1/2 tsp red pepper flakes.  These additions just make the meal more substantial.

This is my go-to Vodka Sauce recipe. I've tried a few others and they simply don't compare. The pancetta really makes all the difference, so don't skimp. After following the recipe to the T, the first time, I tried to substitute normal bacon on the second go. It simply doesn't compare. Pancetta may be a bit pricey, but it's worth every single penny. I'd also double the vodka. The alcohol content cooks out, leaving a rich flavor behind.

text:
Thank you thank you thank you!  This was better than I imagined.  I didn't have the exact ingredients so improvised.  After browning 14 oz. chopped prosciutto (which I drained) since it was what I had on hand, I added and sauteed about 1/2 diced red onion and about 2 cloves of garlic. I used 1 8 oz. can of tomato sauce and 2 diced roma tomates. Based on other reviews, I decided to increase the amount of sauce and added 1 c. cream and 1 c. milk.  I simmered this with 1 tsp. black pepper and 1 tsp. crushed red pepper.  This sauce, along with the suggested 16 oz. of penne, made about 8 servings...unfortunately, we each ate closer to 2 servings each!  I will probably reduce the prosciutto (or hopefully I will have pancetta on hand) by 1/2 as well as omit the cheese as it was a bit salty for our taste. I'll save this one for an "indulgence meal" as it is so rich...but, man, was it good!  Thanks Rick!

Great sauce! I added some parmesan a bit earlier, and also I cook my pasta a few minutes short of al dente and then add them to the sauce for a few minutes to finish cooking.
